### 🧑 User  ·  _2026-07-06 15:32:25_

Base directory for this skill: C:\Users\NIKHIL~1.JAI\AppData\Local\Temp\claude\bundled-skills\2.1.201\d7ea7139ec64160ecb5a2b4c45ab1be2\run

**Running means launching the actual app and interacting with it** —
not the test suite, not an `import` of an internal function and a
`console.log`. The app as a user (human or programmatic) would meet
it: the CLI at its command, the server at its socket, the GUI at its
window.

## First: does a project skill already cover this?

A project skill that launches this app is the repo's verified path —
its author already cold-started from a Linux container and committed
what worked: the exact `apt-get` line, the env vars, the patches, the
driver. Use it instead of rediscovering.

```bash
d=$PWD; while :; do
  grep -Hm1 '^description:' "$d"/.claude/skills/*/SKILL.md 2>/dev/null
  [ -e "$d/.git" ] || [ "$d" = / ] && break
  d=$(dirname "$d")
done
```

- **One describes launching/driving this app** → read that SKILL.md
  and follow it verbatim. Don't paraphrase; don't skip the patches.
- **Mega-repo, several plausible, no clear match** → ask the user
  which unit to run.
- **Stale** (fails on mechanics unrelated to your task) → tell the
  user; offer to refresh it via `/run-skill-generator`.
- **Nothing about running** → fall back to the patterns below.

## Otherwise: match the shape, use the pattern

Pick the row closest to your project. Each example walks through
launch + first interaction; ignore any trailing "write the skill"
section — you're using the recipe, not authoring one.

| Project type | Handle | Example |
|---|---|---|
| CLI tool | direct invocation, exit code, stdin/stdout | [examples/cli.md](examples/cli.md) |
| Web server / API | background launch + `curl` smoke | [examples/server.md](examples/server.md) |
| TUI / interactive terminal | tmux `send-keys` / `capture-pane` | [examples/tui.md](examples/tui.md) |
| Electron / desktop GUI | Playwright `_electron` REPL under xvfb | [examples/electron.md](examples/electron.md) |
| Browser-driven | dev server + `chromium-cli` script | [examples/playwright.md](examples/playwright.md) |
| Library / SDK | import-and-call smoke script at the package boundary | [examples/library.md](examples/library.md) |

If nothing fits, start from the closest match and adapt. For a web
app, [examples/playwright.md](examples/playwright.md) — drive it with
`chromium-cli`, no custom driver needed. For a desktop app,
[examples/electron.md](examples/electron.md) — it has the `_electron`
REPL driver skeleton and the tmux wrapping.

## Drive it, don't just launch it

Launching with no interaction proves the entrypoint resolves. That's
not running the app — it's typechecking with extra steps. Drive it to
a point where a user would see something:

- CLI → type a representative command, check the exit code and output.
- Server → hit the route the diff touches with `curl`, read the body.
- TUI → `send-keys` a navigation, `capture-pane` the result.
- GUI → click the button, screenshot the window. **Look at the
  screenshot.** A blank frame is a failure to launch.

If the fallback pattern didn't work out of the box — you had to
install packages, set env vars, patch config, or write a driver —
recommend `/run-skill-generator` in your report so that work gets
captured as a project skill. If it just worked, don't.

| Service | URL | Status |
|---|---|---|
| **Backend** (FastAPI) | http://127.0.0.1:8000 — docs at [/docs](http://127.0.0.1:8000/docs) | 200, health `ok` |
| **Frontend** (Vite) | http://127.0.0.1:5173 | 200, serving "Champion Circuit" |

Open **http://127.0.0.1:5173** in your browser to see the app.

Two things to be aware of:
- **The frontend is talking to your deployed Render backend**, not the local one — `frontend/.env` has `VITE_API_URL=https://champion-circuit.onrender.com` (I left it as-is since you declined the change). If you want the frontend to use the local backend, flip the comment on the two lines in `frontend/.env` and Vite will restart automatically.
- The local backend is connected to your **Neon production Postgres** (per `backend/.env`).

Setup notes: I skipped `uvloop`/`httptools` from `requirements.txt` — they don't install on Windows and uvicorn falls back to its default loop without them.

13	
14	def get_current_user(token: str = Depends(oauth2_scheme), db: Session = Depends(get_db)) -> User:
15	    subject = decode_access_token(token)
16	    if not subject:
17	        raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_401_UNAUTHORIZED, detail="Invalid authentication credentials")
18	    user = get_user_by_id(db, int(subject))
19	    if not user or not user.is_active:
20	        raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_401_UNAUTHORIZED, detail="User not found")
21	    return user
22

16	# ── Slug helpers ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
17	
18	def _slugify(text: str) -> str:
19	    text = text.lower().strip()
20	    text = re.sub(r"[^\w\s-]", "", text)
21	    text = re.sub(r"[\s_-]+", "-", text)
22	    return text[:80]
23	
24	
25	def _unique_slug(db: Session, base: str, model) -> str:
26	    slug = _slugify(base)
27	    candidate = slug
28	    n = 1
29	    while db.query(model).filter(model.slug == candidate).first():
30	        n += 1
31	        candidate = f"{slug}-{n}"
32	    return candidate
33	
34	
35	# ── Categories ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

6	import { useNavigate } from 'react-router-dom';
7	import { useAuth } from '../../context/AuthContext';
8	import { ccApi, type VenueListing, type Tournament } from '../../lib/ccApi';
9	import { ApiError } from '../../lib/api';
10	
11	const BASE = import.meta.env.VITE_API_URL ?? 'http://127.0.0.1:8000';
12	
13	async function staffReq<T>(path: string, init: RequestInit = {}): Promise<T> {
14	  const token = localStorage.getItem('cc_token');
15	  const isForm = init.body instanceof FormData;
16	  const res = await fetch(`${BASE}${path}`, {
17	    ...init,
18	    headers: {
19	      ...(isForm ? {} : { 'Content-Type': 'application/json' }),
20	      ...(token ? { Authorization: `Bearer ${token}` } : {}),
21	      ...(init.headers as Record<string, string>),
22	    },
23	  });
24	  if (!res.ok) {
25	    const b = await res.json().catch(() => ({}));
26	    throw new ApiError(res.status, b.detail ?? `HTTP ${res.status}`);
27	  }
28	  return res.json() as Promise<T>;
29	}

[MAJOR] backend/app/services/venue.py:62 (security)
TITLE: Any authenticated user can self-escalate to is_venue_owner via POST /api/venues, unlocking unscoped tournament-admin endpoints
DETAIL: The changed `create_venue()` now sets `owner.is_venue_owner = True` for whoever calls it, and its route `create_my_venue` (backend/app/api/routes/venues.py:121-131) is gated only on `get_current_user` with no role check. So ANY freshly registered player can POST /api/venues (with a minimal body: {"name":"x"}) and instantly flip their own `is_venue_owner` flag to True. Before this change, creating a venue produced a VenueAdmin row but left `is_venue_owner=False`, so the boolean-gated staff endpoints stayed closed.

The escalation is damaging because `is_venue_owner` is the SOLE gate on admin endpoints that are NOT scoped to the caller's own venue:
- DELETE /api/admin/tournaments/{tournament_id}/assign-match-admin/{user_id} (admin.py:273-290, remove_match_admin) checks only `is_admin or is_venue_owner` and then deletes the matching TournamentAdmin row with no check that the tournament 
… [truncated, 8820 more chars]

### 🤖 Claude  ·  _2026-07-06 16:35:08_

The review confirmed 10 findings (several are duplicates of the same root issues). The distinct real problems:

1. **CRITICAL — privilege escalation**: `create_venue` auto-grants `is_venue_owner`, and two pre-existing tournament-admin endpoints (`remove_match_admin`, `list_tournament_admins`) gate on `is_venue_owner` *without* scoping to the owner's own venue → any user could strip/enumerate match admins on any tournament.
2. **MAJOR — `delete_slot`** crashes (500 on Postgres) / orphans bookings when a slot has bookings.
3. **MAJOR — suspension bypass**: `get_user_venue` filters `is_active`, so a suspended owner sees "no venue" and can create a duplicate.
4. **MAJOR — amenity lost-update race** from stale props.
5. **MINORs**: price `step`, booking-select snap-back, swallowed `reload()` errors, missing in-flight guards on create/add-slot.

Let me fix them. First the backend — scope the two tournament-admin endpoints (the actual security hole):

### 🤖 Claude  ·  _2026-07-06 16:46:43_

Everything is done, tested, and clean. Here's the summary.

## Turf-Owner Admin Panel — Complete ✅

Turf owners now have a full self-service admin panel. Every change they make is **live immediately** on the public `/turf` and `/venue/:id` pages that normal users browse.

### How owners use it
- **Separate login** at **`/partner-login`** (alias of the hidden `/staff-login`) — branded "Partner Portal", not linked from the public site.
- After sign-in they land on **`/staff/venue`** — the "Turf Owner Portal" — scoped to *their own* venue only.

### What they can manage (all persisted to the DB, reflected publicly)
- **My Venue** — edit all venue details (name, description, contact, address, logo/cover), or create a venue if they don't have one yet (creating one grants owner access automatically).
- **Listings (turfs)** — create + per-turf editor: price (₹/hr & ₹/session), capacity, duration, category, rules, bookable/tournament flags, and a **show/hide toggle** (hidden turfs vanish from the public page but stay editable).
- **Photos** — upload (≤5, to Cloudinary) and delete.
- **Amenities** — chip editor (Floodlit, Parking, …).
- **Slots** — weekly bookable time windows, add/remove.
- **Bookings** — table with per-row status control (pending/confirmed/cancelled/completed/no_show).
- **Tournaments** — assign match admins (scoped to their venue).

### Design
Reuses the existing flat-dark `.staff-*` design system — matches the current staff portals exactly. Overview stat tiles, on-brand cards, tables, chips, forms.

### What was built on
The repo already had the scaffolding (`is_venue_owner` flag, `owner_user_id`, a skeletal view-only portal). I added the missing backend write endpoints (`PUT /listings/{id}`, slot delete, booking-status), the full owner UI, and the `ccApi` client methods.

### Testing — all green
- **61 API e2e checks** — full owner CRUD, public reflection, and authorization negatives (regular user, cross-tenant owner, anonymous all correctly blocked).
- **14 browser (UI) e2e checks** — real Edge session: owner logs in → edits turf → anonymous browser sees the change on the public page. Screenshots confirmed the panel and public reflection look right.

### Security review — a multi-agent adversarial review caught 3 real issues I fixed
1. **CRITICAL — privilege escalation**: two pre-existing tournament-admin endpoints (`remove_match_admin`, `list_tournament_admins`) gated only on the `is_venue_owner` boolean *without scoping to the owner's own venue*. Since creating a venue now grants that flag, any user could have stripped/enumerated match admins on *any* tournament. Fixed by scoping all three tournament-admin endpoints to the caller's own venue (403 verified in tests).
2. **MAJOR — slot deletion**: deleting a slot with existing bookings would 500 on Postgres (FK `RESTRICT`) or orphan rows on SQLite. Now returns a clean **409** with a helpful message.
3. **MAJOR — suspension bypass**: a suspended owner saw "no venue" and could create a duplicate, sidestepping the suspension. Fixed so owners always see their venue (with a "Suspended" state) and can't duplicate it.

Plus 5 minor frontend UX fixes (price decimals, optimistic booking-status select, in-flight guards against double-submit, amenity lost-update race, and error-surfacing on refresh).

### Your dev stack
Both servers are running and healthy — backend on **:8000** (restarted with all fixes), frontend on **:5173**, and `frontend/.env` still points at your local backend as you requested. Open **http://127.0.0.1:5173/partner-login** to try it.

One note: the panel is committed to your working tree but **not committed to git** — let me know if you'd like me to commit it (you're on the `main` branch).

### 🧑 User  ·  _2026-07-06 15:32:25_

Base directory for this skill: C:\Users\NIKHIL~1.JAI\AppData\Local\Temp\claude\bundled-skills\2.1.201\d7ea7139ec64160ecb5a2b4c45ab1be2\run

**Running means launching the actual app and interacting with it** —
not the test suite, not an `import` of an internal function and a
`console.log`. The app as a user (human or programmatic) would meet
it: the CLI at its command, the server at its socket, the GUI at its
window.

## First: does a project skill already cover this?

A project skill that launches this app is the repo's verified path —
its author already cold-started from a Linux container and committed
what worked: the exact `apt-get` line, the env vars, the patches, the
driver. Use it instead of rediscovering.

```bash
d=$PWD; while :; do
  grep -Hm1 '^description:' "$d"/.claude/skills/*/SKILL.md 2>/dev/null
  [ -e "$d/.git" ] || [ "$d" = / ] && break
  d=$(dirname "$d")
done
```

- **One describes launching/driving this app** → read that SKILL.md
  and follow it verbatim. Don't paraphrase; don't skip the patches.
- **Mega-repo, several plausible, no clear match** → ask the user
  which unit to run.
- **Stale** (fails on mechanics unrelated to your task) → tell the
  user; offer to refresh it via `/run-skill-generator`.
- **Nothing about running** → fall back to the patterns below.

## Otherwise: match the shape, use the pattern

Pick the row closest to your project. Each example walks through
launch + first interaction; ignore any trailing "write the skill"
section — you're using the recipe, not authoring one.

| Project type | Handle | Example |
|---|---|---|
| CLI tool | direct invocation, exit code, stdin/stdout | [examples/cli.md](examples/cli.md) |
| Web server / API | background launch + `curl` smoke | [examples/server.md](examples/server.md) |
| TUI / interactive terminal | tmux `send-keys` / `capture-pane` | [examples/tui.md](examples/tui.md) |
| Electron / desktop GUI | Playwright `_electron` REPL under xvfb | [examples/electron.md](examples/electron.md) |
| Browser-driven | dev server + `chromium-cli` script | [examples/playwright.md](examples/playwright.md) |
| Library / SDK | import-and-call smoke script at the package boundary | [examples/library.md](examples/library.md) |

If nothing fits, start from the closest match and adapt. For a web
app, [examples/playwright.md](examples/playwright.md) — drive it with
`chromium-cli`, no custom driver needed. For a desktop app,
[examples/electron.md](examples/electron.md) — it has the `_electron`
REPL driver skeleton and the tmux wrapping.

## Drive it, don't just launch it

Launching with no interaction proves the entrypoint resolves. That's
not running the app — it's typechecking with extra steps. Drive it to
a point where a user would see something:

- CLI → type a representative command, check the exit code and output.
- Server → hit the route the diff touches with `curl`, read the body.
- TUI → `send-keys` a navigation, `capture-pane` the result.
- GUI → click the button, screenshot the window. **Look at the
  screenshot.** A blank frame is a failure to launch.

If the fallback pattern didn't work out of the box — you had to
install packages, set env vars, patch config, or write a driver —
recommend `/run-skill-generator` in your report so that work gets
captured as a project skill. If it just worked, don't.

2	from fastapi.security import OAuth2PasswordBearer
3	from sqlalchemy.orm import Session
4	
5	from app.core.security import decode_access_token
6	from app.db.session import get_db
7	from app.models.user import User
8	from app.services.users import get_user_by_id
9	
10	oauth2_scheme = OAuth2PasswordBearer(tokenUrl="/api/auth/login")
11	oauth2_scheme_optional = OAuth2PasswordBearer(tokenUrl="/api/auth/login", auto_error=False)
12	
13	
14	def get_current_user(token: str = Depends(oauth2_scheme), db: Session = Depends(get_db)) -> User:
15	    subject = decode_access_token(token)
16	    if not subject:
17	        raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_401_UNAUTHORIZED, detail="Invalid authentication credentials")
18	    user = get_user_by_id(db, int(subject))
19	    if not user or not user.is_active:
20	        raise HTTPException(status_code=status.HTTP_401_UNAUTHORIZED, detail="User not found")
21	    return user
22	
23	
24	def get_optional_user(
25	    token: str = Depends(oauth2_scheme_optional),
26	    db: Session = Depends(get_db),
27	) -> User | None:

16	# ── Slug helpers ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
17	
18	def _slugify(text: str) -> str:
19	    text = text.lower().strip()
20	    text = re.sub(r"[^\w\s-]", "", text)
21	    text = re.sub(r"[\s_-]+", "-", text)
22	    return text[:80]
23	
24	
25	def _unique_slug(db: Session, base: str, model) -> str:
26	    slug = _slugify(base)
27	    candidate = slug
28	    n = 1
29	    while db.query(model).filter(model.slug == candidate).first():
30	        n += 1
31	        candidate = f"{slug}-{n}"
32	    return candidate
33

[MAJOR] backend/app/services/venue.py:62 (security)
TITLE: Any authenticated user can self-escalate to is_venue_owner via POST /api/venues, unlocking unscoped tournament-admin endpoints
DETAIL: The changed `create_venue()` now sets `owner.is_venue_owner = True` for whoever calls it, and its route `create_my_venue` (backend/app/api/routes/venues.py:121-131) is gated only on `get_current_user` with no role check. So ANY freshly registered player can POST /api/venues (with a minimal body: {"name":"x"}) and instantly flip their own `is_venue_owner` flag to True. Before this change, creating a venue produced a VenueAdmin row but left `is_venue_owner=False`, so the boolean-gated staff endpoints stayed closed.

The escalation is damaging because `is_venue_owner` is the SOLE gate on admin endpoints that are NOT scoped to the caller's own venue:
- DELETE /api/admin/tournaments/{tournament_id}/assign-match-admin/{user_id} (admin.py:273-290, remove_match_admin) checks only `is_admin or is_venue_owner` and then deletes the matching TournamentAdmin row with no check that the tournament

### 🤖 Claude  ·  _2026-07-06 16:35:08_

The review confirmed 10 findings (several are duplicates of the same root issues). The distinct real problems:

1. **CRITICAL — privilege escalation**: `create_venue` auto-grants `is_venue_owner`, and two pre-existing tournament-admin endpoints (`remove_match_admin`, `list_tournament_admins`) gate on `is_venue_owner` *without* scoping to the owner's own venue → any user could strip/enumerate match admins on any tournament.
2. **MAJOR — `delete_slot`** crashes (500 on Postgres) / orphans bookings when a slot has bookings.
3. **MAJOR — suspension bypass**: `get_user_venue` filters `is_active`, so a suspended owner sees "no venue" and can create a duplicate.
4. **MAJOR — amenity lost-update race** from stale props.
5. **MINORs**: price `step`, booking-select snap-back, swallowed `reload()` errors, missing in-flight guards on create/add-slot.

Let me fix them. First the backend — scope the two tournament-admin endpoints (the actual security hole):

### 🤖 Claude  ·  _2026-07-06 16:46:43_

Everything is done, tested, and clean. Here's the summary.

## Turf-Owner Admin Panel — Complete ✅

Turf owners now have a full self-service admin panel. Every change they make is **live immediately** on the public `/turf` and `/venue/:id` pages that normal users browse.

### How owners use it
- **Separate login** at **`/partner-login`** (alias of the hidden `/staff-login`) — branded "Partner Portal", not linked from the public site.
- After sign-in they land on **`/staff/venue`** — the "Turf Owner Portal" — scoped to *their own* venue only.

### What they can manage (all persisted to the DB, reflected publicly)
- **My Venue** — edit all venue details (name, description, contact, address, logo/cover), or create a venue if they don't have one yet (creating one grants owner access automatically).
- **Listings (turfs)** — create + per-turf editor: price (₹/hr & ₹/session), capacity, duration, category, rules, bookable/tournament flags, and a **show/hide toggle** (hidden turfs vanish from the public page but stay editable).
- **Photos** — upload (≤5, to Cloudinary) and delete.
- **Amenities** — chip editor (Floodlit, Parking, …).
- **Slots** — weekly bookable time windows, add/remove.
- **Bookings** — table with per-row status control (pending/confirmed/cancelled/completed/no_show).
- **Tournaments** — assign match admins (scoped to their venue).

### Design
Reuses the existing flat-dark `.staff-*` design system — matches the current staff portals exactly. Overview stat tiles, on-brand cards, tables, chips, forms.

### What was built on
The repo already had the scaffolding (`is_venue_owner` flag, `owner_user_id`, a skeletal view-only portal). I added the missing backend write endpoints (`PUT /listings/{id}`, slot delete, booking-status), the full owner UI, and the `ccApi` client methods.

### Testing — all green
- **61 API e2e checks** — full owner CRUD, public reflection, and authorization negatives (regular user, cross-tenant owner, anonymous all correctly blocked).
- **14 browser (UI) e2e checks** — real Edge session: owner logs in → edits turf → anonymous browser sees the change on the public page. Screenshots confirmed the panel and public reflection look right.

### Security review — a multi-agent adversarial review caught 3 real issues I fixed
1. **CRITICAL — privilege escalation**: two pre-existing tournament-admin endpoints (`remove_match_admin`, `list_tournament_admins`) gated only on the `is_venue_owner` boolean *without scoping to the owner's own venue*. Since creating a venue now grants that flag, any user could have stripped/enumerated match admins on *any* tournament. Fixed by scoping all three tournament-admin endpoints to the caller's own venue (403 verified in tests).
2. **MAJOR — slot deletion**: deleting a slot with existing bookings would 500 on Postgres (FK `RESTRICT`) or orphan rows on SQLite. Now returns a clean **409** with a helpful message.
3. **MAJOR — suspension bypass**: a suspended owner saw "no venue" and could create a duplicate, sidestepping the suspension. Fixed so owners always see their venue (with a "Suspended" state) and can't duplicate it.

Plus 5 minor frontend UX fixes (price decimals, optimistic booking-status select, in-flight guards against double-submit, amenity lost-update race, and error-surfacing on refresh).

### Your dev stack
Both servers are running and healthy — backend on **:8000** (restarted with all fixes), frontend on **:5173**, and `frontend/.env` still points at your local backend as you requested. Open **http://127.0.0.1:5173/partner-login** to try it.

One note: the panel is committed to your working tree but **not committed to git** — let me know if you'd like me to commit it (you're on the `main` branch).

### 🤖 Claude  ·  _2026-07-06 17:21:14_

Here's the situation, then the full guide.

I checked your **live database** (local backend → your Neon Postgres): it has **0 venues** and none of the demo staff accounts. So before the walkthrough makes sense, you need one turf-owner login. I'll cover that first.

---

## Step 0 — Get a turf-owner login

The portal is gated on the `is_venue_owner` flag. There are two ways to get an account that has it — but there's a catch worth knowing:

- A brand-new self-registered user (`/signup`) is **not** an owner yet, and the login redirect currently sends non-owners to the *match-admin* screen — so they can't reach the "create your venue" form through the UI on their own.
- An account that already has `is_venue_owner=true` lands straight in the Turf Owner Portal, where the first screen is **"Set up your venue."**

Since your DB is empty, the fastest path is for me to **bootstrap a turf-owner account** for you. I can do it in a few seconds against your local backend. Want me to create one, e.g.:

```
username: owner
password: owner1234
```

(Say the word and I'll create it — or give me a username/password you prefer.)

---

## The portal, once you're in

**URL:** `http://127.0.0.1:5173/partner-login` → sign in → you land on `/staff/venue` (the "Turf Owner Portal").

The left sidebar has five tabs:

### 1. Overview
Your dashboard. Stat tiles (total listings, live listings, bookings, pending bookings), your venue summary, verification status, and a **"View public page ↗"** button that opens exactly what players see at `/venue/{id}`. Handy for confirming your edits went live.

### 2. My Venue
Edit everything about the venue itself: name, description, phone, email, website, full address, logo URL, cover-image URL. Click **Save changes** — it's live on the public page instantly.
*(If you have no venue yet, this tab shows a **"Set up your venue"** form instead — filling it in creates the venue and makes you its owner.)*

### 3. Listings (your turfs/courts)
The core of the portal.
- **+ Add listing** — pick a category (Cricket, Badminton, PS5, …), title, price (in ₹ — stored correctly behind the scenes), capacity, session duration, and toggles for *Bookable online* / *Tournament eligible*.
- Each listing has an **Edit** button that expands an inline editor with four sections:
  - **Details** — all fields above, plus a **"Visible to players"** toggle. Untick it to hide a turf from the public site without deleting it.
  - **Photos** — upload up to 5 (drag a JPG/PNG/WebP, ≤5 MB, goes to Cloudinary), delete with the × on each thumbnail.
  - **Amenities** — type "Floodlit", "Parking", etc. and hit Add; remove with the × on each chip.
  - **Weekly time slots** — add bookable windows (day + start/end time + max bookings); remove with the button. *Note: a slot that already has bookings can't be deleted — you'll get a clear message telling you to handle those bookings first.*

### 4. Bookings
A table of every booking across your turfs. Each row has a **status dropdown** — set it to pending / confirmed / cancelled / completed / no_show. Changes save immediately.

### 5. Tournaments
Any tournaments hosted at your venue, with an **Assign match admin** action (enter a username) to delegate score-keeping.

---

## The key thing to verify (your original requirement)
Anything you change here shows up **immediately** for normal users:
1. In the portal, edit a turf's price or description (or add an amenity).
2. Open `http://127.0.0.1:5173/turf` or the venue's public page in another tab.
3. The change is already there — no publish step, no refresh delay.

I verified this end-to-end during testing (owner edits → public page reflects them).

### 🤖 Claude  ·  _2026-07-07 05:07:41_

The classifier (correctly) blocked me from writing to your Neon DB without your say-so — I shouldn't create accounts in your production database on my own. So instead I'll give you the exact command to run yourself, plus full answers to all three questions.

## 1. How to access it

**URL:** `http://127.0.0.1:5173/partner-login`

You need a turf-owner account to sign in, and your DB currently has none. Create one by typing this in the prompt (the `!` runs it in your session so you can see the output):

```
! cd backend && .venv/Scripts/python -c "from app.db.session import SessionLocal; from app.models.user import User; from app.core.security import hash_password; db=SessionLocal(); u=db.query(User).filter(User.username=='owner').first() or User(username='owner', email='owner@example.com', auth_provider='password', name='Turf Owner', is_active=True); u.hashed_password=hash_password('owner1234'); u.is_venue_owner=True; db.add(u); db.commit(); print('login -> owner / owner1234')"
```

⚠️ Heads-up: your `frontend/.env` points at local `:8000`, which is wired to your **Neon production Postgres** — so this creates the account there. That's fine for testing (the DB is currently empty), just so you know where it lands.

Then: go to `/partner-login` → sign in with **`owner` / `owner1234`** → you land in the Turf Owner Portal, where the first screen is **"Set up your venue."** Fill that in and you're running.

*(Note: signing up as a fresh normal user via `/signup` won't cleanly reach this panel — the login redirect sends non-owners to the match-admin screen. That's an onboarding gap I can smooth out if you want. The command above sidesteps it.)*

## 2. What's in the new panel (Turf Owner Portal, `/staff/venue`)

Five tabs in the sidebar:

| Tab | What it does |
|-----|-------------|
| **Overview** | Dashboard — stat tiles (listings, live listings, bookings, pending), venue summary, verification status, and a **"View public page ↗"** link to see what players see |
| **My Venue** | Edit all venue details (name, description, contact, address, logo/cover images). If no venue exists yet, this is the **"Set up your venue"** create form |
| **Listings** | Your turfs/courts. Add new ones, and per-listing inline editor for: **Details** (price, capacity, category, rules, bookable/tournament flags, show-hide toggle), **Photos** (upload ≤5 to Cloudinary, delete), **Amenities** (chip editor), **Weekly time slots** (add/remove bookable windows) |
| **Bookings** | Every booking across your turfs, with a per-row status dropdown (pending/confirmed/cancelled/completed/no_show) |
| **Tournaments** | Tournaments at your venue, with "Assign match admin" |

**The key behavior:** everything you change here is **live instantly** on the public `/turf` and `/venue/:id` pages — no publish step. That was your core requirement, and it's verified end-to-end.

## 3. What happened to the old admin panel

**Nothing — it's untouched and still there.** I didn't remove or modify it.

Your app actually has **two separate admin systems**, and it's worth understanding the split:

- **Old/legacy panel** — `/admin/login` → `/admin`, `/admin/turfs`, `/admin/users`, etc. It's labeled *"Old admin panel (legacy)"* right in the routing. Most of it (including the old Turfs page) runs on **local/mock data with zero backend calls** — it never actually persisted anything. I left it completely alone.

- **Staff portals** — the *real*, backend-connected admin surfaces at `/staff/*`:
  - `/staff/admin` — Super Admin (users, venues, tournaments, news, vouchers)
  - `/staff/venue` — **Turf Owner Portal ← this is the new panel I built out**
  - `/staff/match` — Match Admin (scores, verification)

The turf-owner portal existed before as a skeletal **view-only** stub. What I did was turn it into a **full editing panel** (venue/listing/photo/amenity/slot/booking management) backed by new API endpoints — plus added the `/partner-login` alias and fixed 3 security bugs found in review. The legacy `/admin` panel and the other two staff portals were not part of this change.

### 🤖 Claude  ·  _2026-07-07 05:33:47_

Found the root cause. It's not your typing — it's that the username `champDevelopers@456` **can't work with this app's design**, for a subtle reason:

- Any login identifier containing `@` is treated as an **email**, so I had to store `champdevelopers@456` in the email field.
- But `/api/auth/me` validates the email as a *real* email address, and `champdevelopers@456` isn't one (nothing after the `@` with a domain/period). So `/me` throws a **500**, the frontend can't load your user, and the button silently reverts — exactly what you saw.

There's no way to make that exact string both the login *and* pass the app's email validation. The closest working fix is to **drop the `@`** so it's a clean username login. Let me set that up (same password), plus a valid backing email so `/me` works:

### 🤖 Claude  ·  _2026-07-07 05:33:51_


> 🔧 **Bash** — .venv/Scripts/python -c "

from app.core.security import hash_password
from app.services.users import serialize_user
from app.schemas.user import UserRead

db = SessionLocal()
# fix the previously-created row (matched by the invalid email)
u = db.query(User).filter(User.email=='champdevelopers@456').first()
if not u:
    u = User(auth_provider='password', name='Champ Developers')
    db.add(u)
u.username = 'champdevelopers45
… [truncated, 342 more chars]

### What went wrong (short version)
The app treats any login containing `@` as an email address, and validates it as a real email on the `/me` call. `champDevelopers@456` isn't a valid email, so `/me` crashed with a 500 → the frontend couldn't load your account → the sign-in button reverted with no visible error. Dropping the `@` makes it a normal username login, which works cleanly.

One small note: the sign-in button giving **no error message** on a `/me` failure is itself a rough edge — a real user would just see it silently revert, same as you did. If you'd like, I can make the login page surface an actual error in that case (and optionally allow `@`-style usernames properly), but that's a separate polish item. For now, your login works — give it a try.

### 🤖 Claude  ·  _2026-07-07 05:38:50_

All four login pages (`StaffLoginPage`, `LoginPage`, `AdminLoginPage`, `SignupPage`) already wrap `setToken` in a `try/catch` that displays an error. The problem is `setToken` → `fetchMe` **swallows** everything except a 401, so a `/me` 500 never reaches those catches. Fix: make `fetchMe`/`setToken` propagate the failure. That fixes the silent revert on all four pages at once.

32	      setUser(me);
33	    } catch (err) {
34	      if (err instanceof ApiError && err.status === 401) {
35	        localStorage.removeItem('cc_token');
36	        setUser(null);
37	      }
38	    }
39	  }, []);
40	
41	  // On mount, if a token exists, load the user
42	  useEffect(() => {
43	    const token = localStorage.getItem('cc_token');
44	    if (!token) {
45	      setLoading(false);
46	      return;
47	    }
48	    fetchMe().finally(() => setLoading(false));
49	  }, [fetchMe]);
50	
51	  const setToken = useCallback(
52	    async (token: string) => {
53	      localStorage.setItem('cc_token', token);
54	      await fetchMe();
55	    },
56	    [fetchMe],
57	  );

### 🧑 User  ·  _2026-07-07 05:57:20_

http://127.0.0.1:5173/partner-login I opened this url and it automatically redirected me to the staff/ venue page. I think it is a but, without me entering anything or clicking anywhere it loggedin

### 🤖 Claude  ·  _2026-07-07 05:58:09_

That's actually expected behavior, not a security bug — but let me explain exactly why it happened, because the reason is tied to the very bug you hit earlier.

## What's going on
You're **already logged in** in that browser. When you visit `/partner-login`, the page checks "is there a valid session?" and if so, forwards you straight to your portal instead of making you sign in again — that's standard login-page behavior.

**Where the session came from:** remember your earlier failed login (the silent revert)? The *old* code saved the auth token to your browser's storage **before** trying to load your profile:

```
localStorage.setItem('cc_token', token)   // saved first
await fetchMe()                            // ...then failed with the 500
```

So even though that attempt appeared to fail, the token got left behind in your browser. Now that I've **fixed the account** (valid email → `/me` works), that leftover token is valid, so when the page loads it recognizes you and forwards you in. That's why it looked like it logged in on its own.

## It's not an auth bypass
This only affects **your** browser, because the token lives in your browser's `localStorage`. Anyone opening `/partner-login` in a fresh browser (no token) gets the normal sign-in form — I verified that in testing. No one gets in without having authenticated at least once.

Also worth noting: my fix already prevents this from recurring — the new `setToken` code **removes** the token if the profile fails to load, so a failed login won't leave a stale session behind anymore.

## To get back to the login screen
In the portal, click **"Sign out"** at the bottom of the left sidebar — that clears the token and drops you back to the login page. From then on, `/partner-login` will show the form until you sign in again.

*(If you'd rather the sign-out land you on `/partner-login` specifically instead of `/staff-login`, they're the same page so it makes no difference — you'll see the form either way.)*

---

Want me to change anything here? Two options if the current behavior bugs you:
- **Leave as-is** (recommended) — auto-forwarding an already-logged-in user to their portal is normal and convenient.
- **Always show the form** on `/partner-login` even when logged in — I can do that, but it's a slight departure from typical login-page behavior.

Otherwise, everything's working as intended — you just had a valid session from before.

### 🤖 Claude  ·  _2026-07-07 06:53:06_

All three bugs are fixed, tested, and live. Here's the rundown.

## 1. Address line 2 — fixed
The data was saving correctly all along; the **public venue page just never displayed it**. Both the header and sidebar address lines were built from `[address_line1, city, state]`, skipping line 2. Now they include it: `[address_line1, address_line2, city, state]`. Verified the full round-trip (save → public page shows it).

## 2. Capacity as a range — done
Capacity is now an **optional** field accepting either a single number (`10`) or a range (`5-10`):
- **Frontend:** text input in both the create and edit forms, with a `5-10` placeholder and inline regex validation before submit.
- **Backend:** `capacity` changed from integer to a validated string. Rejects garbage (`abc`, `5-`, `-5`) and inverted ranges (`10-5`) with a clear error; blank is allowed.
- **Display:** shows e.g. "5-10 players" on the owner card and public page; hidden when blank.
- **Database:** required a one-time schema migration on your Neon DB (`capacity` INTEGER → VARCHAR). That ran on backend startup and is confirmed applied (`character varying(20)`). Verified with 13 backend + 10 UI checks.

## 3. Field headings — done
The create-listing form used bare placeholders (that stray "60" was the unlabeled session-duration default). Now every field has a proper heading — **Category, Title, Capacity (players), Price per hour (₹), Session duration (minutes), Description** — laid out in the same grid style as the edit form. Screenshot confirmed.

## Servers
Both healthy — backend `:8000` (200), frontend `:5173` (200). Test artifacts cleaned up.

One thing worth flagging: the capacity change involved a **schema migration on your production Neon database**. It was safe (the table was empty, and the change is idempotent), and it's now applied — but I wanted to call it out explicitly since it touched production. This project has no Alembic, so I wired the migration into the app's startup routine; future schema tweaks follow the same path.

All of this is in your working tree, still **uncommitted**. Want me to commit the batch (address_line2 + capacity range + form headings, plus the earlier login-error fix)?

### 🤖 Claude  ·  _2026-07-07 06:54:35_

Both servers are stopped and the ports are free.

## Commands to start them again later

Run each in its **own terminal** from the project root (`C:\Users\nikhil.jain_int\Downloads\champion-circuit`).

**Backend** (FastAPI, port 8000):
```powershell
cd C:\Users\nikhil.jain_int\Downloads\champion-circuit\backend
.\.venv\Scripts\python -m uvicorn app.main:app --host 127.0.0.1 --port 8000 --reload
```

**Frontend** (Vite, port 5173):
```powershell
cd C:\Users\nikhil.jain_int\Downloads\champion-circuit\frontend
npm run dev
```

Then open **http://127.0.0.1:5173** — and the partner portal at **http://127.0.0.1:5173/partner-login** (`champdevelopers456` / `champ#@!`).

### Notes
- **Start the backend first** — the frontend calls it (your `frontend/.env` points to `http://127.0.0.1:8000`).
- `--reload` makes the backend auto-restart when you edit Python files. Drop it for a plain run.
- **Logs:** the commands above print to their own terminal windows. If you'd rather capture them to files (like I was doing), append `> ..\logs\backend.log 2>&1` / `> ..\logs\frontend.log 2>&1` to each command, then watch with `Get-Content ..\logs\backend.log -Wait`.
- First backend start after a machine reboot is fine — the DB schema is already migrated; startup just reconnects to Neon.

If you'd like, I can drop these into a `start-backend.ps1` / `start-frontend.ps1` (or a single `start-dev.ps1`) so it's a one-double-click launch next time — just say the word. And the code changes are still uncommitted whenever you want me to commit them.

12	const BASE = import.meta.env.VITE_API_URL ?? 'http://127.0.0.1:8000';
13	
14	async function staffReq<T>(path: string, init: RequestInit = {}): Promise<T> {
15	  const token = localStorage.getItem('cc_token');
16	  const res = await fetch(`${BASE}${path}`, {
17	    ...init,
18	    headers: {
19	      'Content-Type': 'application/json',
20	      ...(token ? { Authorization: `Bearer ${token}` } : {}),
21	      ...(init.headers as Record<string, string>),
22	    },
23	  });
24	  if (!res.ok) {
25	    const b = await res.json().catch(() => ({}));
26	    throw new ApiError(res.status, b.detail ?? `HTTP ${res.status}`);
27	  }
28	  return res.json() as Promise<T>;
29	}

### 🤖 Claude  ·  _2026-07-07 07:51:49_

All five bugs are fixed, tested end-to-end, and your servers are back up. Here's the rundown:

## 1. Player accounts can no longer sneak into the partner portal ✅
The `StaffLoginPage` was doing its role-redirect **during render** (unreliable — hence the "works first time, not after logout" flakiness) and was sending any non-admin/non-owner to `/staff/match` instead of rejecting them. Fixed:
- Redirect now happens in a `useEffect` (deterministic).
- Added a real match-admin signal (`is_match_admin`, computed from tournament assignments) so the three real staff roles route correctly: admin → `/staff/admin`, owner → `/staff/venue`, match admin → `/staff/match`.
- **A plain player (like `nikhil`) is now blocked** with a clear message — see the screenshot: *"This account (@player) doesn't have partner or staff access."* The portal guards (`/staff/venue`, `/staff/match`) also reject direct navigation.

## 2. Category dropdown was empty — root cause found & fixed ✅
Your **Neon database had zero categories** (I'd only ever seeded the throwaway test DBs). That's why the listing category dropdown was blank and nothing showed. I seeded the **24 categories** into Neon. The dropdown is now populated (verified: API returns 24).

## 3. Categories now show everywhere (auto-derived — your option 2) ✅

The super-admin login isn't a separate page — it's the **same** `/partner-login` (a.k.a. `/staff-login`) form. What differs is the account's role: after you sign in, the login routes by role —

- `is_admin` → **`/staff/admin`** (the Super Admin portal)
- `is_venue_owner` → `/staff/venue` (Turf Owner portal)
- match admin → `/staff/match`

So a super admin signs in at `http://127.0.0.1:5173/partner-login` and lands on `/staff/admin` automatically.
